margin-left: 0; text-align: left; font-size: 105%; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit;"><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0">&#160;\n  </li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flag_of_Ecuador.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ecuador.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flag_of_Ecuador.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ecuador.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flag_of_Ecuador.svg/45px-Flag_of_Ecuador.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1440" data-file-height="960" />&#160;</span>Ecuador\n  </li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span>Taiwan</li></ul>\n</div>\n &#160;</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Establishment</th><td>\n1971</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>RIMPAC</b>, the <b>Rim of the Pacific Exercise</b>, is the world\'s largest international maritime <a href="/wiki/Military_exercise" title="Military exercise">warfare exercise</a>. RIMPAC is held <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/biennial" class="extiw" title="wikt:biennial">biennially</a> during June and July of even-numbered years from <a href="/wiki/Honolulu" title="Honolulu">Honolulu</a>, Hawaii. It is hosted and administered by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/United_States_Pacific_Fleet" title="United States Pacific Fleet">Pacific Fleet</a>, headquartered at <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor" title="Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a>, in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">Marine Corps</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">Coast Guard</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_National_Guard" title="Hawaii National Guard">Hawaii National Guard</a> forces under the control of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Hawaii" title="List of Governors of Hawaii">Governor of Hawaii</a>. The US invites military forces from the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Rim" title="Pacific Rim">Pacific Rim</a> and beyond to participate. With RIMPAC the United States Pacific Command seeks to enhance interoperability among Pacific Rim armed forces, ostensibly as a means of promoting stability in the region to the benefit of all participating nations. Described by the US Navy as a unique training opportunity that helps participants foster and sustain the cooperative relationships that are critical to ensuring the safety of sea lanes and security on the world\'s oceans.<sup id="cite_ref-CPFRIMPAC2014_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPFRIMPAC2014-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Participants"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Participants">Participants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exercise_RIMPAC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Participants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Abraham-Lincoln-battlegroup.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Abraham-Lincoln-battlegroup.jpg/220px-Abraham-Lincoln-battlegroup.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Abraham-Lincoln-battlegroup.jpg/330px-Abraham-Lincoln-battlegroup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Abraham-Lincoln-battlegroup.jpg/440px-Abraham-Lincoln-battlegroup.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2030" data-file-height="1297" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Abraham-Lincoln-battlegroup.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/USS_Abraham_Lincoln_(CVN-72)" title="USS Abraham Lincoln (CVN-72)">USS <i>Abraham Lincoln</i></a> <a href="/wiki/Carrier_battle_group" title="Carrier battle group">carrier battle group</a> along with ships from Australia, Canada, Chile, Japan, and South Korea during RIMPAC 2000.</div></div></div>\n<p>The first RIMPAC, held in 1971, involved forces from Australia, Canada, New Zealand, the United Kingdom (UK), and the United States (US). Australia, Canada, and the US have participated in every RIMPAC since then. Other regular participants are Chile, Colombia, France, Indonesia, Japan, Malaysia, the Netherlands, Peru, Singapore, South Korea, and Thailand. The <a href="/wiki/Royal_New_Zealand_Navy" title="Royal New Zealand Navy">Royal New Zealand Navy</a> was frequently involved until the 1985 <a href="/wiki/ANZUS" title="ANZUS">ANZUS</a> nuclear ships dispute, but has taken part in recent RIMPACs such as in 2012, 2014, 2016 and 2018.\n</p><p>Several observer nations are usually invited, including China, Ecuador, India, Mexico, the Philippines, and Russia, who became an active participant for the first time in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Russia_2012_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Russia_2012-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> While not contributing any ships, observer nations are involved in RIMPAC at the strategic level and use the opportunity to prepare for possible full participation in the future.\n</p><p>The United States contingent has included an <a href="/wiki/Carrier_strike_group" title="Carrier strike group">aircraft carrier strike group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarines</a>, up to a hundred aircraft and 20,000 Sailors, <a href="/wiki/US_Marines" class="mw-redirect" title="US Marines">Marines</a>, Coast Guardsmen and their respective officers. The size of the exercises varies from year to year.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="RIMPAC_2004">RIMPAC 2004</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a submarines, 100 aircraft, and nearly 18,000 military personnel from seven navies, including Canada, Australia, Japan, South Korea, Chile, and the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-Ships_of_RIMPAC_2004_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ships_of_RIMPAC_2004-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Submarines_of_RIMPAC_2004_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Submarines_of_RIMPAC_2004-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Aircraft_of_RIMPAC_2004_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aircraft_of_RIMPAC_2004-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It focused on multinational training while building trust and cooperation among the participating naval partners. Rear Admiral <a href="/wiki/Patrick_M._Walsh" title="Patrick M. Walsh">Patrick M. Walsh</a>, Commander <a href="/wiki/Carrier_Strike_Group_Seven" class="mw-redirect" title="Carrier Strike Group Seven">Carrier Group Seven</a>, served as Multinational Task Force Commander<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> aboard the aircraft carrier <a href="/wiki/USS_John_C._Stennis" title="USS John C. Stennis">USS&#160;<i>John C. Stennis</i></a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="RIMPAC_2010">RIMPAC 2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="3495" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_100719-N-7042V-107_Royal_Australian_Navy_Leading_Seaman_Livingston_Harrison,_foreground,_U.S._Navy_Lt._j.g._Joe_Spence_and_Columbian_navy_Lt._Cmdr._Anibal_Limbo_stand_watch_in_Sea_Combat_Control_a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sea Combat Control (19 July 2010)</div></div></div>\n<p>On 23 June 2010, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Pacific_Fleet" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Pacific Fleet">U.S. Pacific Fleet</a> commander Admiral <a href="/wiki/Patrick_M._Walsh" title="Patrick M. Walsh">Patrick M. Walsh</a> and Combined Task Force commander Vice Admiral <a href="/wiki/Richard_W._Hunt" title="Richard W. Hunt">Richard W. Hunt</a> announced the official start of the month-long 2010 Rim of the Pacific (RIMPAC) exercise during a press conference held in Lockwood Hall at <a href="/wiki/Joint_Base_Pearl_Harbor-Hickam" class="mw-redirect" title="Joint Base Pearl Harbor-Hickam">Joint Base Pearl Harbor-Hickam</a>. RIMPAC 2010 was the 22nd exercise in the series that originated in 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-NNS100629-22_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NNS100629-22-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The exercise was designed to increase the operational and tactical proficiency of participating units in a wide array of maritime operations by enhancing military-to-military relations and interoperability.<sup id="cite_ref-NNS100802-16_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NNS100802-16-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Thirty-two ships, five submarines, over 170 aircraft, and 20,000 personnel participated in RIMPAC 2010, the world\'s largest multi-national maritime exercise.<sup id="cite_ref-NNS100808-01_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NNS100808-01-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>RIMPAC 2010 brought together units and personnel from Australia, Canada, Chile, Colombia, France, Indonesia, Japan, Malaysia, Netherlands, Peru, South Korea, Singapore, Thailand, and the United States. During the exercise, participating countries conducted gunnery, missile, anti-submarine, and air defense exercises, as well as maritime interdiction and vessel boarding, explosive ordnance disposal, diving and salvage operations, mine clearance operations, and an amphibious landing. RIMPAC 2010 will also emphasize <a href="/wiki/Littoral_zone" title="Littoral zone">littoral</a> operations with ships like the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Littoral_combat_ship" title="Littoral combat ship">littoral combat ship</a> <a href="/wiki/USS_Freedom_(LCS-1)" title="USS Freedom (LCS-1)"><i>Freedom</i></a>, the French frigate <a href="/wiki/French_frigate_Prairial" title="French frigate Prairial"><i>Prairial</i></a>, and the Singaporean <a href="/wiki/Formidable-class_frigate" title="Formidable-class frigate"><i>Formidable</i>-class&#x20;frigate</a> RSS <i>Supreme</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-NNS100629-22_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NNS100629-22-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 June 2010, the aircraft carrier <a href="/wiki/USS_Ronald_Reagan_(CVN-76)" class="mw-redirect" title="USS Ronald Reagan (CVN-76)"><i>Ronald Reagan</i></a> arrived in Pearl Harbor to participate in RIMPAC 2010. <i>Ronald Reagan</i> was the only aircraft carrier to participate in this exercise. During the in-port phase of RIMPAC, officers and crew of the 14 participating navies interact in receptions, meetings, and athletic events.<sup id="cite_ref-CVN74history2010_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CVN74history2010-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <i>Ronald Reagan</i> completed its Tailored Ships Training Availability (TSTA) exercises prior to RIMPAC 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-CVN74history2010_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CVN74history2010-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During 6\xe2\x80\x937 July 2010, 32 naval vessels and five submarines from seven nations departed Pearl Harbor to participate in Phase II of RIMPAC 2010. This phase included live fire gunnery and missile exercises; maritime interdiction and vessel boardings; and anti-surface warfare, undersea warfare, naval maneuvers and air defense exercises. Participants also collaborated in explosive ordnance disposal; diving and salvage operations; mine clearance operations; and amphibious operations.<sup id="cite_ref-NNS100708-18_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NNS100708-18-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Phase III involved scenario-driven exercises designed to further strengthen maritime skills and capabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-NNS100708-18_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NNS100708-18-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During RIMPAC 2010, over 40 naval personnel from Singapore, Japan, Australia, Chile, Peru, and Colombia managed combat exercises while serving aboard <i>Ronald Reagan</i> (pictured). This involved managing anti-submarine warfare and surface warfare for Carrier Strike Group Seven and the entire RIMPAC force, including the use of radar, charts, and high-tech devices to monitor, chart, and communicate with other ships and submarines. Tactical action officers from the different countries coordinated the overall operational picture and provided direction and administration to the enlisted personnel involved in the Sea Combat Control (SCC) activities.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Also, <i>Ronald Reagan</i> conducted a live <a href="/wiki/RIM-116_Rolling_Airframe_Missile" title="RIM-116 Rolling Airframe Missile">Rolling Airframe Missile (RAM)</a> launch, firing at a simulated target, the first since 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-NNS100808-01_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NNS100808-01-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CVN74history2010_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CVN74history2010-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 30 July 2010, RIMPAC 2010 concluded with a press conference held at Merry Point Landing on Joint Base Pearl Harbor-Hickam.<sup id="cite_ref-NNS100802-16_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NNS100802-16-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> A reception for over 1,500 participants, distinguished visitors and special guests was held in the hangar bays of the carrier <i>Ronald Reagan</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-NNS100808-01_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NNS100808-01-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During RIMPAC 2010, participating countries conducted three sinking exercises (SINKEX) involving 140 discrete live-fire events that included 30 surface-to-air engagements, 40 air-to-air missile engagements, 12 surface-to-surface engagements, 76 <a href="/wiki/Laser-guided_bomb" title="Laser-guided bomb">laser-guided bombs</a>, and more than 1,000 rounds of naval gunfire from 20 surface combatant warships.<sup id="cite_ref-NNS100802-16_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NNS100802-16-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Units flew more than 3100 air sorties, completed numerous maritime interdiction and vessel boardings, explosive ordnance disposal, diving and salvage operations and mine clearance operations and 10 major experiments, with the major one being the U.S. Marine Corps Enhanced Company Operations experiment.<sup id="cite_ref-NNS100802-16_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NNS100802-16-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Ground forces from five countries completed five amphibious landings, including nine helicopter-borne amphibious landings and 560 troops from ship-to-shore mission. In all, 960 different training events were scheduled and 96 percent were completed in all areas of the Hawaiian operations area, encompassing <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Base_Hawaii" title="Marine Corps Base Hawaii">K\xc4\x81ne\xca\xbbohe Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bellows_Air_Force_Station" title="Bellows Air Force Station">Bellows Air Force Station</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Missile_Range_Facility" title="Pacific Missile Range Facility">Pacific Missile Range Facility</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pohakuloa_Training_Area" title="Pohakuloa Training Area">Pohakuloa Training Area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NNS100802-16_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NNS100802-16-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" href="/wiki/Auxiliary_ship" title="Auxiliary ship">Auxiliary ships</a>:</b> <br /><a href="/wiki/USNS_Henry_J._Kaiser_(T-AO-187)" title="USNS Henry J. Kaiser (T-AO-187)">USNS&#160;<i>Henry J. Kaiser</i></a><br /><a href="/wiki/USNS_Matthew_Perry_(T-AKE-9)" title="USNS Matthew Perry (T-AKE-9)">USNS&#160;<i>Matthew Perry</i></a><br /><a href="/wiki/USNS_Salvor_(T-ARS-52)" class="mw-redirect" title="USNS Salvor (T-ARS-52)">USNS&#160;<i>Salvor</i></a><br /><a href="/wiki/USNS_Yukon_(T-AO-202)" title="USNS Yukon (T-AO-202)">USNS&#160;<i>Yukon</i></a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>RIMPAC 2012 is the 23rd exercise in the series and started on 29 June 2012. 42 ships, including the aircraft carrier <a href="/wiki/USS_Nimitz" title="USS Nimitz">USS&#160;<i>Nimitz</i></a> and other elements of <a href="/wiki/Carrier_Strike_Group_Eleven" class="mw-redirect" title="Carrier Strike Group Eleven">Carrier Strike Group 11</a>, six submarines,<sup id="cite_ref-vessels_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vessels-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> 200 aircraft and 25,000 personnel from 22 nations took part in Hawaii. The exercise involved surface combatants from the U.S., Canada, Japan, Australia, South Korea and Chile.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The US Navy demonstrated its \'<a href="/wiki/Great_Green_Fleet" title="Great Green Fleet">Great Green Fleet</a>\' of biofuel-driven vessels for which it purchased 450,000 gallons of biofuel, the largest single purchase of biofuel in history at a cost of $12m.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> On 17 July, <a href="/wiki/USNS_Henry_J._Kaiser_(T-AO-187)" title="USNS Henry J. Kaiser (T-AO-187)">USNS&#160;<i>Henry J. Kaiser</i></a> delivered 900,000 gallons of biofuel and traditional petroleum-based fuel to <i>Nimitz</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s Carrier Strike Group 11.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The exercises included units or personnel from Australia, Canada, Chile, Colombia, France, India, Indonesia, Japan, Malaysia, Mexico, Netherlands, New Zealand, Norway, Peru, the Republic of Korea, the Republic of the Philippines, Russia, Singapore, Thailand, Tonga, the United Kingdom and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Russia participated actively for the first time,<sup id="cite_ref-Russia_2012_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Russia_2012-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> as did the Philippines, reportedly due to the escalating tensions with the People\'s Republic of China over ownership of Scarborough Shoal.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>RIMPAC 2012 marked the debut of the U.S. Navy\'s new <a href="/wiki/P-8A_Poseidon" class="mw-redirect" title="P-8A Poseidon">P-8A Poseidon</a> land-based anti-submarine patrol aircraft, with two P-8As participating in 24 RIMPAC exercise scenarios as part of Air Test and Evaluation Squadron One (VX-1) based at <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Base_Hawaii" title="Marine Corps Base Hawaii">Marine Corps Base Hawaii</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kaneohe_Bay" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaneohe Bay">Kaneohe Bay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="RIMPAC_2014">RIMPAC 2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a (MCM-8)">USS&#160;<i>Scout</i></a><br />Mobile Dive Salvage Units<br />Explosive Ordnance Disposal Units<br />Mine Counter Measure Dive Units<br />Marine Mammal Systems\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>RIMPAC 2014 was the 24th exercise in the series and took place from 26 June to 1 August, with an opening reception on 26 June and closing reception 1 August.<sup id="cite_ref-CPFRIMPAC2014_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPFRIMPAC2014-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For the first time, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Norwegian_Navy" title="Royal Norwegian Navy">Royal Norwegian Navy</a> actively participated in the exercise. Norway sent one <a href="/wiki/Fridtjof_Nansen-class_frigate" title="Fridtjof Nansen-class frigate"><i>Fridtjof Nansen</i>-class&#x20;frigate</a> and possibly Norwegian marine special forces.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> China was also invited to send ships from their <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army_Navy" title="People&#39;s Liberation Army Navy">People\'s Liberation Army Navy</a>; marking not only the first time China participated in a RIMPAC exercise, but also the first time China participated in a large-scale United States-led naval drill.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> On 9 June 2014, China confirmed it would be sending four ships to the exercise, a destroyer, frigate, supply ship, and hospital ship.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The year\'s RIMPAC participants were Australia, Brunei, Canada, Chile, China, Colombia, France, India, Indonesia, Japan, Malaysia, Mexico, Netherlands, New Zealand, Norway, Peru, the Philippines, Singapore, South Korea, Tonga, the United Kingdom, and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Thailand was uninvited from the exercise following a 22 May military coup. Thailand\'s absence means that 22 nations participated in RIMPAC instead of the 23 that had been advertised.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The exercise involved 55 vessels, more than 200 aircraft, and some 25,000 personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-RIMPAC2014PF_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIMPAC2014PF-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="RIMPAC_2016">RIMPAC 2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="RIMPAC_2018">RIMPAC 2018</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exercise_RIMPAC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: RIMPAC 2018">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>On 23 May 2018, <a href="/wiki/The_Pentagon" title="The Pentagon">the Pentagon</a> announced that it had "disinvited" China because of recent <a href="/wiki/Territorial_disputes_in_the_South_China_Sea" title="Territorial disputes in the South China Sea">militarization of islands in the South China Sea</a>, after China had announced in January that it had been invited.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>  The PRC has previously attended RIMPAC 2014 &amp; 2016.\n</p><p>On 30 May 2018, the US Kaiser</i></a><br /> <a href="/wiki/USNS_Charles_Drew_(T-AKE-10)" title="USNS Charles Drew (T-AKE-10)">USNS&#160;<i>Charles Drew</i></a><br /> <a href="/wiki/USNS_Carl_Brashear_(T-AKE-7)" title="USNS Carl Brashear (T-AKE-7)">USNS&#160;<i>Carl Brashear</i></a><br /> <a href="/wiki/USNS_Mercy_(T-AH-19)" title="USNS Mercy (T-AH-19)">USNS&#160;<i>Mercy</i></a><br /> <a href="/wiki/USNS_Sioux_(T-ATF-171)" title="USNS Sioux (T-ATF-171)">USNS&#160;<i>Sioux</i></a><br /> HOS <i>Mystique</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Ensign_of_Vietnam_People%27s_Navy.svg/23px-Ensign_of_Vietnam_People%27s_Navy.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Ensign_of_Vietnam_People%27s_Navy.svg/35px-Ensign_of_Vietnam_People%27s_Navy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Ensign_of_Vietnam_People%27s_Navy.svg/46px-Ensign_of_Vietnam_People%27s_Navy.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2017" data-file-height="1326" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Vietnam_People%27s_Navy" title="Vietnam People&#39;s Navy">Vietnam People\'s Navy</a></td>\n<td>Staff\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In this edition of RIMPAC, the <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Navy" title="Chilean Navy">Chilean Navy</a> was responsible for leading the naval exercise, being the first non-English-speaking Navy to carry out this task. The election of <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> as leader of the Task Groups is a recognition of the high performance achieved in recent editions and the quality of its personnel, which since its first participation in 1996 has been demonstrating its preparation and professionalism. His appointment also places this country in a leadership position in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin American">Latin American</a> and world level in the planning and execution of combined naval operations.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> will be making their debut in RIMPAC. <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> was due to make its debut too, but cancelled its participation for the second time.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The exercise will also include a live firing of the <a href="/wiki/LRASM" class="mw-redirect" title="LRASM">LRASM</a> anti-ship missile for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Experiments">Experiments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exercise_RIMPAC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Experiments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>RIMPAC experiments have included a range of sectors important to international militaries. In RIMPAC 2000, for example, the first of the <a href="/wiki/Strong_Angel" title="Strong Angel">Strong Angel</a> international humanitarian response demonstrations was held on the Big Island of Hawai\'i near Pu\'u Pa\'a. That series continued with events in the summer of 2004 and again in 2006.\n</p><p>Participants have also conducted exercises in ship-sinking and torpedo usage. They also have tested new naval vessels and technology. For example, in 2004, the United States Navy tested the Australian built <a href="/wiki/HSV-2_Swift" title="HSV-2 Swift">HSV-2&#160;<i>Swift</i></a>, a 321-foot (98&#160;m) experimental wave-piercing catamaran that draws only 11 feet (3.4&#160;m) of water, has a top speed of almost 50 knots (93&#160;km/h; 58&#160;mph), and can transport 605 tons of cargo.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px"><div style="width: 235px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 230px;"><div style="margin:69px auto;"><a
